<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Royal Rumble</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>Royal Rumble</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestling</a> <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> event, produced every January by <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_promotion" title="Professional wrestling promotion">professional wrestling promotion</a> <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwematch_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwematch-1">[1]</a></sup> The event is named after the Royal Rumble match, a <a href="/wiki/Battle_royal_(professional_wrestling)" title="Battle royal (professional wrestling)">Battle royal</a> match whose participants enter at timed intervals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the exception of the initial Royal Rumble event in 1988, which was shown as a television special on <a href="/wiki/USA_Network" title="USA Network">USA Network</a>, the Royal Rumble has been shown on pay-per-view (first in <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1989)" title="Royal Rumble (1989)">1989</a>) and is one of WWE's "Big Four", along with <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania" title="WrestleMania">WrestleMania</a>, <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam" title="SummerSlam">SummerSlam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series" title="Survivor Series">Survivor Series</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The Royal Rumble is considered one of WWE's most popular pay-per-view events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mysterio_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-mysterio-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Event">Event</span></h3>
<p>The Royal Rumble is a <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> consisting of the Royal Rumble match, title matches, and various other matches. The first Royal Rumble took place on January 24, 1988 and was broadcast live on the <a href="/wiki/USA_Network" title="USA Network">USA Network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RF161_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-RF161-5">[5]</a></sup> The following year, the event started to be broadcast on pay-per-view<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwh_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-pwh-6">[6]</a></sup> and thus became one of WWE's "big four" pay-per-views, along with <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania" title="WrestleMania">WrestleMania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series" title="Survivor Series">Survivor Series</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam" title="SummerSlam">SummerSlam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Main166_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Main166-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Royal Rumble match is usually located at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Card" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">card</a>, though there have been exceptions such as the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1988)" title="Royal Rumble (1988)">1988</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1996)" title="Royal Rumble (1996)">1996</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1997)" title="Royal Rumble (1997)">1997</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1998)" title="Royal Rumble (1998)">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2006)" title="Royal Rumble (2006)">2006</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2013)" title="Royal Rumble (2013)">2013</a> events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guard_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-guard-8">[8]</a></sup> Due to the Rumble match taking up a large amount of time (most Rumble matches last roughly one hour), the Rumble event tends to have a smaller card than most other pay-per-view events, which routinely have six to eight matches per card. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2008)" title="Royal Rumble (2008)">2008 Royal Rumble</a> was the first WWE pay-per-view to be available in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high-definition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rrhd_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-rrhd-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Match">Match</span></h3>
<p>The Royal Rumble is based on the classic <a href="/wiki/Battle_royal_(professional_wrestling)" title="Battle royal (professional wrestling)">Battle Royal</a> match, in which a number of wrestlers (usually 30) aim at eliminating their competitors by tossing them over the top rope, with both feet touching the floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwematch_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-wwematch-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The winner of the event is the last wrestler remaining after all others have been eliminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwematch_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-wwematch-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mysterio_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-mysterio-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Royal Rumble differs from the classical Battle Royal as the contestants do not enter the ring at the same time but instead are assigned entry numbers, usually via a <a href="/wiki/Lottery" title="Lottery">lottery</a>, although desirable spots are occasionally assigned by other means, the most common being winning a match. This lottery is usually staged right before the event begins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwematch_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-wwematch-1">[1]</a></sup> The match begins with the two wrestlers who have drawn entry numbers one and two, with the remaining wrestlers entering the ring at regular timed intervals, either 90 seconds or two minutes, according to their entry number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwematch_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-wwematch-1">[1]</a></sup> This format is credited to <a href="/wiki/Pat_Patterson_(wrestler)" title="Pat Patterson (wrestler)">Pat Patterson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pat_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-pat-11">[11]</a></sup> To date, only four men who have been one of the starting wrestlers have won the Royal Rumble: <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Michaels" title="Shawn Michaels">Shawn Michaels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Benoit" title="Chris Benoit">Chris Benoit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rey_Mysterio" title="Rey Mysterio">Rey Mysterio</a>. The most common number to win is number 27.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Rumble_match.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Royal_Rumble_match.jpg/220px-Royal_Rumble_match.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Royal_Rumble_match.jpg/330px-Royal_Rumble_match.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Royal_Rumble_match.jpg/440px-Royal_Rumble_match.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Rumble_match.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Royal Rumble match in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Royal Rumble match commonly involves 30 wrestlers and usually lasts an hour, with the longest match, at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2002)" title="Royal Rumble (2002)">2002 event</a>, lasting over one hour and nine minutes of a three-hour pay-per-view.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12">[12]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1988)" title="Royal Rumble (1988)">first match</a>, contested in 1988, involved only 20 men,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RR88_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-RR88-13">[13]</a></sup> and lasted 33 minutes of the two-hour broadcast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2011)" title="Royal Rumble (2011)">2011 Royal Rumble</a> had a 40-man field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rr2011_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-rr2011-14">[14]</a></sup> out of whom Alberto Del Rio was victorious.</p>
<p>Although the vast majority of eliminations are caused by active participants, eliminations caused by other means have occurred, and have been ruled legitimate, including self-eliminations (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andre_the_Giant" title="Andre the Giant">Andre the Giant</a> jumping out of the ring after seeing a <a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">snake</a> in 1989, <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a> eliminating himself in 1999 and <a href="/wiki/Drew_Carey" title="Drew Carey">Drew Carey</a> eliminating himself in 2001; however <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">Randy Savage</a>'s jump over the top rope in 1992 was not ruled as self-elimination), elimination from previously-eliminated participants (such as <a href="/wiki/The_Undertaker" title="The Undertaker">The Undertaker</a> eliminating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maven_(wrestler)" title="Maven (wrestler)">Maven</a> in 2002, <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Angle" title="Kurt Angle">Kurt Angle</a> eliminating <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Michaels" title="Shawn Michaels">Shawn Michaels</a> in 2005, Kane eliminating <a href="/wiki/CM_Punk" title="CM Punk">CM Punk</a> in 2014 and <a href="/wiki/The_Wyatt_Family" title="The Wyatt Family">The Wyatt Family</a> eliminating <a href="/wiki/Brock_Lesnar" title="Brock Lesnar">Brock Lesnar</a> in 2016) and elimination from non-participants (such as Brock Lesnar eliminating <a href="/wiki/Bill_Goldberg" title="Bill Goldberg">Goldberg</a> in 2004, <a href="/wiki/Shane_McMahon" title="Shane McMahon">Shane McMahon</a> eliminating Shawn Michaels in 2006 and <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a> eliminating <a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">John Cena</a> in 2011). Furthermore, if an injured wrestler is taken away by medical staff, he can return to the match as long as the match is still ongoing (such as <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Steve_Austin" title="Stone Cold Steve Austin">Steve Austin</a> in 1999 or <a href="/wiki/Roman_Reigns" title="Roman Reigns">Roman Reigns</a> in 2016), but if the match ends without the injured wrestler returning, he is deemed eliminated (such as <a href="/wiki/Scotty_2_Hotty" title="Scotty 2 Hotty">Scotty 2 Hotty</a> in 2005).</p>
<p>Royal Rumble matches are generally stipulated to involve no <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Disqualification" title="Professional wrestling">disqualifications</a>. The only exception involved <a href="/wiki/Dave_Finlay" title="Dave Finlay">Finlay</a> entering the match before his turn to save <a href="/wiki/Hornswoggle" title="Hornswoggle">Hornswoggle</a> in 2008.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize">Prize</span></h3>
<p>Since 1993, the winner of the Royal Rumble match is traditionally awarded a title match for WWE's top championship at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania" title="WrestleMania">WrestleMania</a> – presently, there are two top championships, the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Championship" title="WWE Championship">WWE Championship</a> on <a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown" title="WWE SmackDown">SmackDown</a> and the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Universal_Championship" title="WWE Universal Championship">WWE Universal Championship</a> on <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-about-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_Brand_Extension" title="WWE Brand Extension">brand extension</a> introduced in mid-2002, the 30 entrants from 2003 to 2006 consisted of 15 wrestlers from both the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a> and <a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown" title="WWE SmackDown">SmackDown</a> brands. At first, the winner of the match received a shot at their brand's top champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Starting in 2004, the Rumble winner had the option of challenging any brand's champion. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Benoit" title="Chris Benoit">Chris Benoit</a> switched brands after winning the 2004 Royal Rumble and won the <a href="/wiki/World_Heavyweight_Championship_(WWE)" title="World Heavyweight Championship (WWE)">World Heavyweight Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-about-15">[15]</a></sup> From 2007 to 2010, participants from the <a href="/wiki/ECW_(WWE)" title="ECW (WWE)">ECW</a> brand competed along with the Raw and SmackDown brands, with the <a href="/wiki/ECW_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="ECW World Heavyweight Championship">ECW World Championship</a> added as an option for the winner to challenge for, although no winners ever did.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecwtitle_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecwtitle-17">[17]</a></sup> During ECW's participation, the entries for each brand were not evenly divided.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RR07_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-RR07-18">[18]</a></sup> The brand extension returned in July 2016, and the winner of the Royal Rumble match will now receive a title opportunity for either SmackDown's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_World_Championship" title="WWE World Championship">WWE World Championship</a> or Raw's <a href="/wiki/WWE_Universal_Championship" title="WWE Universal Championship">WWE Universal Championship</a>.</p>
<p>WWE's top championship has been booked as on the line during the Royal Rumble match on two occasions. In 1992, the vacant WWF World Heavyweight Championship was contested in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1992)" title="Royal Rumble (1992)">1992 Royal Rumble match</a>, eventually won by <a href="/wiki/Ric_Flair" title="Ric Flair">Ric Flair</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RR92_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-RR92-19">[19]</a></sup> while in 2016, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Reigns" title="Roman Reigns">Roman Reigns</a>, was scheduled to defend his WWE World Heavyweight Championship as a participant of that year's Royal Rumble match and was entrant number one. This marked the first time that a reigning champion had to defend his title in the match, which was ultimately won by <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a>.</p>
<p>From 2001 to 2007, the Royal Rumble match winner had gone on to win a World Championship title at WrestleMania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12">[12]</a></sup> After winning the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2008)" title="Royal Rumble (2008)">2008</a> match, <a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">John Cena</a> became the first winner to use his championship opportunity at an event (<a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2008)" title="No Way Out (2008)">No Way Out 2008</a>) other than WrestleMania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> He also became the first since The Rock in 2000 to win the Royal Rumble match but fail to win the title in his championship opportunity.</p>
<p>The Royal Rumble winner may also choose to put his championship opportunity on the line in a match. This was first done in 1996, when Shawn Michaels risked his <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XII" title="WrestleMania XII">WrestleMania XII</a> title shot in a match against <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hart" title="Owen Hart">Owen Hart</a> at <a href="/wiki/In_Your_House_6" title="In Your House 6">In Your House 6</a>. The second time was in 1999, when <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Steve_Austin" title="Stone Cold Steve Austin">Stone Cold Steve Austin</a> offered to forfeit his title opportunity to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ray_Traylor" title="Ray Traylor">Big Boss Man</a>, who won third place in the Rumble (Austin was actually the runner-up in that rumble, but the winner, <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a> himself, had voluntarily given up his title opportunity) if McMahon could beat him in a cage match at <a href="/wiki/St._Valentine%27s_Day_Massacre:_In_Your_House" title="St. Valentine's Day Massacre: In Your House">St. Valentine's Day Massacre: In Your House</a>, which Austin would go on to win. The third time was in 2002, when <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Angle" title="Kurt Angle">Kurt Angle</a> convinced <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a> to put his <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_X8" title="WrestleMania X8">WrestleMania X8</a> championship spot on the line at <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2002)" title="No Way Out (2002)">No Way Out</a>, a match which Angle won. However, Triple H would later defeat Angle and regain his WrestleMania championship spot. The fourth time was in 2006, when <a href="/wiki/Randy_Orton" title="Randy Orton">Randy Orton</a> goaded <a href="/wiki/Rey_Mysterio" title="Rey Mysterio">Rey Mysterio</a> into putting his main event spot at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_22" title="WrestleMania 22">WrestleMania 22</a> on the line at <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2006)" title="No Way Out (2006)">No Way Out</a>, a match which Orton won. Mysterio was eventually reinserted into the main event at WrestleMania, making it a triple threat match, and went on to win the World Heavyweight Championship. On the February 25, 2013 edition of <i>Raw</i>, John Cena successfully defended his <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_29" title="WrestleMania 29">WrestleMania 29</a> WWE Championship opportunity in a match against <a href="/wiki/CM_Punk" title="CM Punk">CM Punk</a>. On February 22, 2015 at <a href="/wiki/Fastlane_(2015)" title="Fastlane (2015)">Fastlane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Reigns" title="Roman Reigns">Roman Reigns</a> defended his <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_31" title="WrestleMania 31">WrestleMania 31</a> WWE World Heavyweight Championship opportunity against <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bryan" title="Daniel Bryan">Daniel Bryan</a>.</p>
<p>In 2000, The Rock was declared the victor, as the storyline intended. However, it was later revealed that his feet had actually touched before those of The Big Show. A singles match was held at <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2000)" title="No Way Out (2000)">No Way Out</a>, the event following the Royal Rumble, to determine who received the Wrestlemania title shot against the reigning champion Triple H. Big Show won with the help of Shane McMahon. Rock then defeated Big Show in a rematch in March on <i>Raw</i> with the help of Vince McMahon, which earned him a title shot and converted the match at WrestleMania into a triple-threat that was later made a four-way match when Linda McMahon inserted the recently retired Mick Foley into the match.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-PPV_Royal_Rumble_matches">Non-PPV Royal Rumble matches</span></h3>
<p>WWE has booked several Royal Rumble matches outside of the annual Royal Rumble event:</p>
<ul>
<li>The first Royal Rumble match broadcast outside of its pay-per-view was a Tag Team Royal Rumble on June 15, 1998. Kane and Mankind won the match and earned an opportunity for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="World Tag Team Championship">WWF Tag Team Championship</a> against the <a href="/wiki/The_New_Age_Outlaws" title="The New Age Outlaws">The New Age Outlaws</a>.</li>
<li>On January 11, 1999, a "Corporate Royal Rumble" involving members of <a href="/wiki/The_Corporation_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Corporation (professional wrestling)">The Corporation</a> and D-Generation X was held on <i>Raw</i> to determine the 30th entry in the Royal Rumble that year. The match was won by <a href="/wiki/Chyna" title="Chyna">Chyna</a>, who last eliminated <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Mr. McMahon</a>.</li>
<li>A 15-man Royal Rumble was held during the January 29, 2004 edition of SmackDown to crown a contender for <a href="/wiki/Brock_Lesnar" title="Brock Lesnar">Brock Lesnar</a>'s <a href="/wiki/WWE_Championship" title="WWE Championship">WWE Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2004)" title="No Way Out (2004)">No Way Out</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Guerrero" title="Eddie Guerrero">Eddie Guerrero</a> won the match, last eliminating <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Angle" title="Kurt Angle">Kurt Angle</a>.</li>
<li>On January 14, 2008, Mr. McMahon organized a mini-Royal Rumble, involving midget wrestlers. Hornswoggle won the match.</li>
<li>On the January 31, 2011 episode of <i>Raw</i>, a Royal Rumble to crown the contender for <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a>'s WWE Championship at <a href="/wiki/Elimination_Chamber_(2011)" title="Elimination Chamber (2011)">Elimination Chamber</a> was held. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lawler" title="Jerry Lawler">Jerry Lawler</a> won the match, last eliminating <a href="/wiki/Sheamus" title="Sheamus">Sheamus</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>WWE has also booked two Royal Rumble matches which were never televised, both in 1994. The first, a 30-man Royal Rumble on January 17, was won by <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hart" title="Owen Hart">Owen Hart</a>, last eliminating <a href="/wiki/Rikishi_(wrestler)" title="Rikishi (wrestler)">Fatu</a>. The second, an 18-man Royal Rumble match, took place on May 9 in <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka, Japan</a> and was won by <a href="/wiki/The_Undertaker" title="The Undertaker">The Undertaker</a>, who last eliminated <a href="/wiki/Bam_Bam_Bigelow" title="Bam Bam Bigelow">Bam Bam Bigelow</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-eliminated_wrestlers">Non-eliminated wrestlers</span></h4>
<p>Several times, wrestlers were drawn to compete in the match but did not actually compete. Their participation is counted as zero seconds, with the exception of #6 Hornswoggle:</p>
<ol>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_Royal_Rumble" title="1991 Royal Rumble">1991</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">"Macho King" Randy Savage</a> was drawn 18th, but no-showed due to leaving the building after costing <a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Warrior" title="The Ultimate Warrior">Ultimate Warrior</a> the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Championship" title="WWE Championship">WWF Championship</a> against <a href="/wiki/Sgt._Slaughter" title="Sgt. Slaughter">Sgt. Slaughter</a>.</li>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_Royal_Rumble" title="1994 Royal Rumble">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shaw" title="Mike Shaw">Bastion Booger</a> was drawn 25th, but no-showed due to suffering food poisoning before the match.</li>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1998_Royal_Rumble" title="1998 Royal Rumble">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Harris_Brothers" title="The Harris Brothers">Skull</a> was drawn 22nd, but no-showed due to being attacked by <a href="/wiki/Los_Boricuas" title="Los Boricuas">Los Boricuas</a> after being mistaken as <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Steve_Austin" title="Stone Cold Steve Austin">Stone Cold Steve Austin</a>.</li>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Royal_Rumble" title="2004 Royal Rumble">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spike_Dudley" title="Spike Dudley">Spike Dudley</a> was drawn 13th, but was attacked on the ramp by <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a></li>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2005_Royal_Rumble" title="2005 Royal Rumble">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotty_2_Hotty" title="Scotty 2 Hotty">Scotty 2 Hotty</a> was drawn 15th, but was attacked on the ramp by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Hassan_(wrestler)" title="Muhammad Hassan (wrestler)">Muhammad Hassan</a>.</li>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Royal_Rumble" title="2008 Royal Rumble">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hornswoggle" title="Hornswoggle">Hornswoggle</a> was drawn 9th and eliminated <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a>, however he wasn't brought into the ring until towards the end of the match by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Henry" title="Mark Henry">Mark Henry</a> and was saved by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Finlay" title="Dave Finlay">Finlay</a> and escorted to the back and never reentered the match.</li>
<li>In 2008, Finlay was drawn 27th, but was disqualified after coming out before his number came up and using his shillelagh to help Hornswoggle.</li>
<li>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_Royal_Rumble" title="2015 Royal Rumble">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Axel" title="Curtis Axel">Curtis Axel</a> was drawn 6th, but attacked on the ramp by <a href="/wiki/Erick_Rowan" title="Erick Rowan">Erick Rowan</a>.</li>
</ol>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_box_set">Video box set</span></h2>
<p>In March 2007, WWE released a complete DVD box set titled <i>Royal Rumble: The Complete Anthology</i>, which showcases every Royal Rumble event in its entirety, up to the 2007 Royal Rumble.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
